âº Perfect! All LSL processes are now stopped. âœ…

  What Happens When You Exit This Session

  YES, exiting this coding session will ensure all coding-related LSL processes are stopped:

  1. This Claude Code session ending will trigger the enhanced-transcript-monitor to stop (when Claude Code
  closes)
  2. No LSL processes will be running after exit (verified - registry is clean)
  3. Next time you start a coding session, it will:
    - Load the NEW fixed code from the scripts
    - Start fresh enhanced-transcript-monitor with getProjectPath() fix
    - Prevent duplicate coordinators with the new registration logic
    - Clean up dead PIDs before registering

  1. Exit this Claude Code session (type exit or close the terminal)
  2. Restart your coding session normally with coding or coding --claude
  3. New processes will use fixed code automatically

**User Request:** trying to launch claude via our coding/bin/coding launcher fails:\
âº Perfect! All LSL processes are now stopped. âœ…

  What Happens When You Exit This Session

  YES, exiting this coding session will ensure all coding-related LSL processes are stopped:

  1. This Claude Code session ending will trigger the enhanced-transcript-monitor to stop (when Claude Code
  closes)
  2. No LSL processes will be running after exit (verified - registry is clean)
  3. Next time you start a coding session, it will:
    - Load the NEW fixed code from the scripts
    - Start fresh enhanced-transcript-monitor with getProjectPath() fix
    - Prevent duplicate coordinators with the new registration logic
    - Clean up dead PIDs before registering

  To Complete the Fix

  1. Exit this Claude Code session (type exit or close the terminal)
  2. Restart your coding session normally with coding or coding --claude
  3. New processes will use fixed code automatically

  What the Fixes Will Prevent

  After restart with the new code:
  - âœ… LSL files will ONLY be created in /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/
  - âœ… NO files will be created in test directories like ~/Agentic/coding-tmp/coding
  - âœ… NO orphaned processes will accumulate
  - âœ… Duplicate monitors/coordinators will be blocked with clear errors

**User Request:** trying to launch claude via our coding/bin/coding launcher fails:\
âº Perfect! All LSL processes are now stopped. âœ…

  What Happens When You Exit This Session

  YES, exiting this coding session will ensure all coding-related LSL processes are stopped:

  1. This Claude Code session ending will trigger the enhanced-transcript-monitor to stop (when Claude Code
  closes)
  2. No LSL processes will be running after exit (verified - registry is clean)
  3. Next time you start a coding session, it will:
    - Load the NEW fixed code from the scripts
    - Start fresh enhanced-transcript-monitor with getProjectPath() fix
    - Prevent duplicate coordinators with the new registration logic
    - Clean up dead PIDs before registering

  To Complete the Fix

  1. Exit this Claude Code session (type exit or close the terminal)
  2. Restart your coding session normally with coding or coding --claude
  3. New processes will use fixed code automatically

  What the Fixes Will Prevent

  After restart with the new code:
  - âœ… LSL files will ONLY be created in /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/
  - âœ… NO files will be created in test directories like ~/Agentic/coding-tmp/coding
  - âœ… NO orphaned processes will accumulate
  - âœ… Duplicate monitors/coordinators will be blocked with clear errors

  The test directory issue you just encountered will not happen again after the restart!

### Read - 2025-11-15 05:23:38 UTC [06:23:38 CEST]

**User Request:** trying to launch claude via our coding/bin/coding launcher fails:\
âº Perfect! All LSL processes are now stopped. âœ…

  What Happens When You Exit This Session

  YES, exiting this coding session will ensure all coding-related LSL processes are stopped:

  1. This Claude Code session ending will trigger the enhanced-transcript-monitor to stop (when Claude Code
  closes)
  2. No LSL processes will be running after exit (verified - registry is clean)
  3. Next time you start a coding session, it will:
    - Load the NEW fixed code from the scripts
    - Start fresh enhanced-transcript-monitor with getProjectPath() fix
    - Prevent duplicate coordinators with the new registration logic
    - Clean up dead PIDs before registering

  To Complete the Fix

  1. Exit this Claude Code session (type exit or close the terminal)
  2. Restart your coding session normally with coding or coding --claude
  3. New processes will use fixed code automatically

  What the Fixes Will Prevent

  After restart with the new code:
  - âœ… LSL files will ONLY be created in /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/
  - âœ… NO files will be created in test directories like ~/Agentic/coding-tmp/coding
  - âœ… NO orphaned processes will accumulate
  - âœ… Duplicate monitors/coordinators will be blocked with clear errors

  The test directory issue you just encountered will not happen again after the restart!

> /exit

### Edit - 2025-11-15 05:23:38 UTC [06:23:38 CEST]

**User Request:** trying to launch claude via our coding/bin/coding launcher fails:\
âº Perfect! All LSL processes are now stopped. âœ…

  What Happens When You Exit This Session

  YES, exiting this coding session will ensure all coding-related LSL processes are stopped:

  1. This Claude Code session ending will trigger the enhanced-transcript-monitor to stop (when Claude Code
  closes)
  2. No LSL processes will be running after exit (verified - registry is clean)
  3. Next time you start a coding session, it will:
    - Load the NEW fixed code from the scripts
    - Start fresh enhanced-transcript-monitor with getProjectPath() fix
    - Prevent duplicate coordinators with the new registration logic
    - Clean up dead PIDs before registering

  To Complete the Fix

  1. Exit this Claude Code session (type exit or close the terminal)
  2. Restart your coding session normally with coding or coding --claude
  3. New processes will use fixed code automatically

  What the Fixes Will Prevent

  After restart with the new code:
  - âœ… LSL files will ONLY be created in /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/
  - âœ… NO files will be created in test directories like ~/Agentic/coding-tmp/coding
  - âœ… NO orphaned processes will accumulate
  - âœ… Duplicate monitors/coordinators will be blocked with clear errors

  The test directory issue you just encountered will not happen again after the restart!

> /exit

**User Request:** trying to launch claude via our coding/bin/coding launcher fails:\
âº Perfect! All LSL processes are now stopped. âœ…

  What Happens When You Exit This Session

  YES, exiting this coding session will ensure all coding-related LSL processes are stopped:

  1. This Claude Code session ending will trigger the enhanced-transcript-monitor to stop (when Claude Code
  closes)
  2. No LSL processes will be running after exit (verified - registry is clean)
  3. Next time you start a coding session, it will:
    - Load the NEW fixed code from the scripts
    - Start fresh enhanced-transcript-monitor with getProjectPath() fix
    - Prevent duplicate coordinators with the new registration logic
    - Clean up dead PIDs before registering

  To Complete the Fix

  1. Exit this Claude Code session (type exit or close the terminal)
  2. Restart your coding session normally with coding or coding --claude
  3. New processes will use fixed code automatically

  What the Fixes Will Prevent

  After restart with the new code:
  - âœ… LSL files will ONLY be created in /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/
  - âœ… NO files will be created in test directories like ~/Agentic/coding-tmp/coding
  - âœ… NO orphaned processes will accumulate
  - âœ… Duplicate monitors/coordinators will be blocked with clear errors

**User Request:** trying to launch claude via our coding/bin/coding launcher fails:\
âº Perfect! All LSL processes are now stopped. âœ…

  What Happens When You Exit This Session

  YES, exiting this coding session will ensure all coding-related LSL processes are stopped:

  1. This Claude Code session ending will trigger the enhanced-transcript-monitor to stop (when Claude Code
  closes)
  2. No LSL processes will be running after exit (verified - registry is clean)
  3. Next time you start a coding session, it will:
    - Load the NEW fixed code from the scripts
    - Start fresh enhanced-transcript-monitor with getProjectPath() fix
    - Prevent duplicate coordinators with the new registration logic
    - Clean up dead PIDs before registering

  To Complete the Fix

  1. Exit this Claude Code session (type exit or close the terminal)
  2. Restart your coding session normally with coding or coding --claude
  3. New processes will use fixed code automatically

  What the Fixes Will Prevent

  After restart with the new code:
  - âœ… LSL files will ONLY be created in /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/
  - âœ… NO files will be created in test directories like ~/Agentic/coding-tmp/coding
  - âœ… NO orphaned processes will accumulate
  - âœ… Duplicate monitors/coordinators will be blocked with clear errors

  The test directory issue you just encountered will not happen again after the restart!

> /exit

âº Perfect! All LSL processes are now stopped. âœ…

  What Happens When You Exit This Session

  YES, exiting this coding session will ensure all coding-related LSL processes are stopped:

  1. This Claude Code session ending will trigger the enhanced-transcript-monitor to stop (when Claude Code
  closes)
  2. No LSL processes will be running after exit (verified - registry is clean)
  3. Next time you start a coding session, it will:
    - Load the NEW fixed code from the scripts
    - Start fresh enhanced-transcript-monitor with getProjectPath() fix
    - Prevent duplicate coordinators with the new registration logic
    - Clean up dead PIDs before registering

  To Complete the Fix

  1. Exit this Claude Code session (type exit or close the terminal)
  2. Restart your coding session normally with coding or coding --claude
  3. New processes will use fixed code automatically

  After restart with the new code:
  - âœ… LSL files will ONLY be created in /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/
  - âœ… NO files will be created in test directories like ~/Agentic/coding-tmp/coding
  - âœ… NO orphaned processes will accumulate
  - âœ… Duplicate monitors/coordinators will be blocked with clear errors

### Bash - 2025-11-15 05:37:19 UTC [06:37:19 CEST]

**User Request:** why did you see CODING_REPO (in THIS shell... i. e. the one running the coding session in ~/Agentic/coding) be set to our installation test folder ~/Agentic/coding-tmp/coding? Does running the install.sh script in that test folder set the env var in all shells? In this case, we'd create a mess, as we would have broken the independence of all coding sessions. Normally, this should not happen, as a user would only ever install coding once on each machine. But if they don't (as is the case just now, during testing of the startup/installation behavior of coding itself), the last run of install.sh would control where the LSL system writes to. This seems to be the root of the problem we just found (and you tried to fix with your latest changes) - reflect and propose a better way of handling this (if one exists)

  "new_string": "detect_platform() {\n    case \"$(uname -s)\" in\n        Darwin*)\n            PLATFORM=\"macos\"\n            ;;\n        Linux*)\n            PLATFORM=\"linux\"\n            ;;\n        MINGW*|CYGWIN*|MSYS*)\n            PLATFORM=\"windows\"\n            ;;\n        *)\n            echo -e \"${RED}Unsupported platform: $(uname -s)${NC}\"\n            exit 1\n            ;;\n    esac\n\n    # Detect actual shell in use (prefer accuracy over platform defaults)\n    if [[ -n \"$SHELL\" ]]; ### Bash - 2025-11-15 05:56:15 UTC [06:56:15 CEST]

**User Request:** # Read session logs for continuity

Read the last session log for continuity. If 3 is given, read the last 3 session log files from both local and coding project histories.

## Steps - Non-Coding Projects (e.g., nano-degree, curriculum-alignment)

1. Infer current project name from working directory path (pwd)
2. Find and read the newest (n) local .specstory/history/*.md files using ls -t
3. Find and read the latest (n) coding/.specstory/history/*_from-<project>.md files using ls -t
4. Summarize sessions to provide continuity of awareness and actions

## Steps - Coding Project

1. Confirm we're in coding project (pwd shows /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding)
2. Find and read the newest (n) local .specstory/history/*.md files (WITHOUT _from- postfix) using ls -t
3. Find and read ALL redirected files from ALL projects:
   - coding/.specstory/history/*_from-nano-degree.md (last n)
   - coding/.specstory/history/*_from-curriculum-alignment.md (last n)
   - coding/.specstory/history/*_from-*.md (any other projects, last n each)
4. Summarize all sessions to provide comprehensive continuity across all project work

## Implementation Notes

- Project name can be inferred from pwd (e.g., /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/nano-degree â†’ nano-degree)
- Session filenames follow pattern: `YYYY-MM-DD_HHMM-HHMM_<userid-hash>.md`
- Cross-project logs: `YYYY-MM-DD_HHMM-HHMM_<userid-hash>_from-<project>.md`
- Local sessions in current project's .specstory/history directory
- Redirected sessions in /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/ directory
- Use `ls -t` to find newest files (already auto-approved)
- Focus on understanding both local and cross-project work completed

## Auto-Approval Note

Use ONLY auto-approved commands: pwd, ls -t
Avoid: git commands, basename - these may trigger approval prompts

## Expected Behavior

### In Non-Coding Projects

When executed, Claude Code should:

1. **Determine current project name** from directory path
2. **Find local session logs** in current project's .specstory/history/
3. **Find redirected logs** in coding/.specstory/history/\*_from-PROJECT.md (where PROJECT is current project name)

### In Coding Project

1. **Determine current project name** from directory path
2. **Find local session logs** in current project's .specstory/history/
3. **Find redirected logs** in coding/.specstory/history/\*_from-PROJECT.md (where PROJECT is current project name)
4. **Read and summarize** the most recent (n) logs from both sources
5. **Present combined summary** showing both local and redirected work

### In Coding Project

When executed, Claude Code should:

1. **Confirm coding project** from directory path
2. **Find local coding logs** WITHOUT _from- postfix (regular coding sessions)
3. **Find ALL redirected logs** from all projects (*_from-*.md)
4. **Read last (n) from each source** (n local coding + n per redirected project)
5. **Present comprehensive summary** showing:
   - Direct coding infrastructure work
   - Cross-project work done from all projects
   - Holistic view of all development activities

## Steps - Non-Coding Projects (e.g., nano-degree, curriculum-alignment)

1. Infer current project name from working directory path (pwd)
2. Find and read the newest (n) local .specstory/history/*.md files using ls -t
3. Find and read the latest (n) coding/.specstory/history/*_from-<project>.md files using ls -t
4. Summarize sessions to provide continuity of awareness and actions

## Steps - Coding Project

1. Confirm we're in coding project (pwd shows /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding)
2. Find and read the newest (n) local .specstory/history/*.md files (WITHOUT _from- postfix) using ls -t
3. Find and read ALL redirected files from ALL projects:
   - coding/.specstory/history/*_from-nano-degree.md (last n)
   - coding/.specstory/history/*_from-curriculum-alignment.md (last n)
   - coding/.specstory/history/*_from-*.md (any other projects, last n each)
4. Summarize all sessions to provide comprehensive continuity across all project work

## Implementation Notes

- Project name can be inferred from pwd (e.g., /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/nano-degree â†’ nano-degree)
- Session filenames follow pattern: `YYYY-MM-DD_HHMM-HHMM_<userid-hash>.md`
- Cross-project logs: `YYYY-MM-DD_HHMM-HHMM_<userid-hash>_from-<project>.md`

- Redirected sessions in /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/.specstory/history/ directory

- Focus on understanding both local and cross-project work completed
